Topic: Logic
Context: The basis of life-the main component of protein is an amino acid molecule.It is an organic molecule.Although people have not directly observed amino acid molecules in cosmic space, scientists have used hydrogen, water, oxygen, methane and formaldehyde in the laboratory to simulate the natural conditions of space.Kinds of amino acids.The raw materials used to synthesize amino acids are abundant in interstellar molecules.It is not difficult to imagine that there must also be amino acid molecules in the universe.As long as there is an appropriate environment, they may be transformed into proteins and further develop into organic life.According to this speculation, there are living bodies on other planets than the earth, and may even be living bodies with higher intelligence.
Question: Which of the following is true to best refute the above speculation?
Choices:
  A: There is a huge difference between the process of developing from protein to organic life and the process from organic molecules to protein
  B: Higher intelligence is not only a product of material evolution, but also a product of continuous socialization
  C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event
  D: Some interstellar molecules are not found in the Earth ’s environment, and they are still not available in the laboratory
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The speculation is that there may be living bodies on other planets with higher intelligence.
  We need to find a statement that can refute this speculation.
  A talks about the difference between the process of developing from protein to organic life and the process from organic molecules to protein, but does not address the speculation.
  B talks about the origin of higher intelligence, but does not address the speculation.
  C talks about the probability of synthesizing amino acid molecules in the natural environment, which may weaken the speculation.
  D talks about some interstellar molecules that are not available in the laboratory, but does not address the speculation.
  Thus, C is the most relevant statement that can refute the speculation that there may be living bodies on other planets with higher intelligence.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Logic
Context: Placebo effect" refers to the phenomenon of letting patients take fake drugs that have no effect at all without knowing it, but they can get the same or better effects than real drugs.The "placebo effect" has been supported by many clinical studies.One explanation for this phenomenon is that human expectations for the future will change the physiological state of the brain, which in turn will cause physiological changes throughout the body.
Question: The following statements can support the above explanation, except
Choices:
  A: The placebo effect is the result of a combination of factors.
  B: Placebo has no effect on Alzheimer's patients who have lost their expected future abilities.
  C: Some patients do not believe that the treatment will be effective.Although they have been treated normally, their condition has worsened.
  D: Inject the subject with normal saline and make him believe that it is an analgesic.The subject's brain then secretes the analgesic endorphin.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The given explanation of the placebo effect is that human expectations for the future change the physiological state of the brain which causes physiological changes throughout the body.
  To support this explanation, we need to find a statement that describes a different cause of the placebo effect.
  Option A does not contradict this explanation, as the statement mentions that the placebo effect is the result of a combination of factors, which could include human expectations for the future.
  Option C supports the given explanation, as it describes that patients who did not believe that the treatment would be effective did not experience the placebo effect.
  Option D also supports the given explanation, as it describes how the subject's belief that they received an analgesic caused their brain to secrete endorphins.
  Option B contradicts the given explanation, as it describes a situation where the placebo effect did not work because the patients had lost their expected future abilities, which would not have changed their physiological state or caused physiological changes throughout the body.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Placebo has no effect on Alzheimer's patients who have lost their expected future abilities.

Context: There are 6 scholars F, G, J, L, M, and N, who will speak at a logical meeting, and the speeches are arranged in the following order? (1) Each speaker speaks only once, and only once at the same time By.(2) Three speakers speak before lunch, and the other three speak after lunch.(3) G must speak before lunch.(4) Only one speaker is between M and N.(5) F speaks in the first or third place.
Question: If the speeches of M and N are separated by lunch, which of the following lists all speakers that can be arranged between M and N?
Choices:
  A: G, J
  C: F, G, J
  B: J, L
  D: F, G, J, L
Response 0:
Thought: 
  M and N are separated by lunch.
  There is only one speaker between M and N.
  Therefore, either M or N speaks before lunch and the other speaks after lunch.
  G must speak before lunch, so M and N speak after lunch.
  F speaks in the first or third place, so F cannot be between M and N.
  Therefore, only J and L can be arranged between M and N.
  The answer is B: J, L.

Thought:

  If N _ M, then one of them speaks after lunch and the other before lunch.
  G must speak before lunch, so G can't be between M and N if they speak consecutively.
  F speaks in the first or third place, so F can't be between M and N if they speak consecutively.
  Therefore, the only possible speaker(s) between M and N are J and L.
  The answer is B: J, L.

Topic: Logic
Context: There are five stations set up from west to east along a section of the high-speed railway along the river.It is known that Fuyi Station is east of Haoyun Station and West of Huyao Station, and is adjacent to Huyao Station; Jiushang Station is adjacent to Yinling Station.
Question: If Haoyun Station is adjacent to Yinling Station, you can get?
Choices:
  A: Yinling is standing west of Haoyun Station
  B: Fuyi standing west of Jiushang Station
  C: Hao Yun stands west of Yinling Station
  D: Jiu Shang standing west of Fuyi Station
Response 0:
Thought:
  Fuyi Station is east of Haoyun Station and west of Huyao Station.
  Fuyi Station is adjacent to Huyao Station.
  Jiushang Station is adjacent to Yinling Station.
  If Haoyun Station is adjacent to Yinling Station, then Haoyun Station and Yinling Station must be next to each other.
  Therefore, Yinling Station must be either to the west or east of Haoyun Station.
  If Yinling Station is to the west of Haoyun Station, then the order from west to east would be: Jiushang, Yinling, Haoyun, Fuyi, Huyao. 
  If Yinling Station is to the east of Haoyun Station, then the order from west to east would be: Jiushang, Haoyun, Yinling, Fuyi, Huyao.
  Therefore, we cannot determine which station is to the west of the other.
  Option A is not correct.
  Option B is not correct.
  Option C is not correct.
  Option D is not correct.
  The answer is None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

(1) If X is F accompaniment, then W is L accompaniment.(2) If X is not a G accompaniment, then Y is an M accompaniment.(3) X or Y is H accompaniment.(4) F and G do not share accompaniment; L and K do not share accompaniment; H and M do not share accompaniment.
Question: It is impossible for Y to accompany the following pair of singers?
Choices:
  A: G and H
  B: L and H
  C: F and L
  D: F and M
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We can use the process of elimination to determine which pairs of singers Y cannot accompany.
  According to condition (2), if X is not a G accompaniment, then Y is an M accompaniment.
  Therefore, if Y is not an M accompaniment, then X must be a G accompaniment.
  According to condition (1), if X is F accompaniment, then W is L accompaniment.
  Therefore, if Y is not an M accompaniment and X is a G accompaniment, then W must be an L accompaniment.
  According to condition (4), L and K do not share accompaniment. Therefore, Y cannot accompany L and K.
  According to condition (3), X or Y is H accompaniment. Therefore, either X or Y must accompany H.
  If Y accompanies H, then Y cannot accompany L (because W must accompany L). Therefore, Y cannot accompany the pair L and H.
  The only remaining option is for X to accompany H. Therefore, Y cannot accompany F and M, as X cannot be an accompaniment for either F or G.
  Therefore, it is impossible for Y to accompany the pair F and M.
  The answer is D: F and M.

  A: Those women who often eat celery pay more attention to fitness, and fitness consumes a lot of physical energy, is very tired, and suppresses the aggressive mood.

Topic: Logic
Context: The report of the Ministry of Health shows that the cost of health care has indeed increased over the years.It can be seen that the medical conditions enjoyed by each of us have greatly improved.
Question: Which of the following raises the most serious question to the above conclusion?
Choices:
  A: The vast majority of health care costs are spent on high-tech intensive care for high-risk patients.
  B: Without increasing costs, our health conditions may also improve.
  C: 70% of the state's allocation to the health sector is for infrastructure construction.
  D: The cost of care for elderly chronic diseases is very large.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The conclusion is that the cost of health care has increased while the medical conditions have improved.
  Option A suggests that most of the health care costs are spent on high-tech intensive care for high-risk patients. This raises a serious question because it suggests that the cost increase may not have led to an overall improvement in medical conditions for everyone, but rather only for a select group of patients.
  Option B suggests that it may be possible to improve health conditions without increasing costs. This is a valid point, but it does not necessarily contradict the conclusion.
  Option C suggests that a large portion of the state's allocation to the health sector is for infrastructure construction. This is not directly related to the conclusion and does not raise a serious question.
  Option D suggests that the cost of care for elderly chronic diseases is very large. This is a valid point, but it does not necessarily contradict the conclusion.
  Therefore, the answer is A: The vast majority of health care costs are spent on high-tech intensive care for high-risk patients.

Context: European fern is a poisonous wild grass that has spread and destroyed many pastures in the northern hemisphere in recent years.One way to deal with this wild grass is to spend less money and be self-sustaining by introducing the natural enemy of this plant.Therefore, some scientists suggested that the moths that feed on the European fern produced in the southern hemisphere were released into the northern hemisphere affected by this wild grass to control the growth of the European fern.
Question: If the scientist ’s proposal to control the European fern is adopted, which of the following is necessary for its success?
Choices:
  A: This northern fern of the northern hemisphere also grows in areas with similar climate and soil conditions in the southern hemisphere.
  B: In addition to eating European ferns, the moths they stock also eat other wild grasses that grow in the northern hemisphere.
  C: The stocked moths can survive in the northern hemisphere and can form a large enough group to reduce the number of European ferns and prevent their growth.
  D: When the number of European ferns decreases, livestock will become immune to diseases caused by this wild grass.
Response 0:
Thought:

  Therefore, the correct answer is C: The stocked moths can survive in the northern hemisphere and can form a large enough group to reduce the number of European ferns and prevent their growth.

Question: Which of the following statements is the logical inference above?

  B: No one can be allowed to stop flying.

  Therefore, the logical inference above is that if a person can realize that there is a danger of flying, it shows that he is mentally normal.
  The answer is C: If a person can realize that there is a danger of flying, it shows that he is mentally normal.

Question: If the following statement is true, which one best explains the strange phenomenon of insurance companies competing for strong insurance business?
Choices:
  A: In 2011, 3 of the 36 companies undertaking compulsory insurance were profitable in this type of insurance.
  B: In the payment of compulsory insurance, some vehicles are paid too much, and some cases that should not be paid are awarded.
  C: Tractors enjoy the agricultural benefit policy, and many places register "transport vehicles" as "tractors", thereby enjoying low tax rates.
  D: Commercial auto insurance is lucrative, and car owners usually do not insure compulsory insurance and commercial auto insurance separately.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The phenomenon is that insurance companies are competing for strong insurance business despite suffering losses.
  The correct answer should explain why insurance companies are still interested in strong insurance business despite losses.
  Options A, C, and D do not provide a clear explanation for why insurance companies are still interested in strong insurance business despite losses.
  Option B suggests that some vehicles are overpaid while some should not be paid at all. This means that insurance companies may still be able to make a profit from strong insurance business by overcharging some customers and avoiding paying out to others.
  Therefore, the best answer is B: In the payment of compulsory insurance, some vehicles are paid too much, and some cases that should not be paid are awarded.
Action: Answer("B")

Context: Some of the students enrolled in the fall of 2007 in colleges and universities are free teachers.All the free normal students are poor.All students from poor families participated in the work-study program.
Question: If the above statement is true, then the following must be true, except
Choices:
  A: Some of the students enrolled in the fall of 2007 were poor..
  B: Students who do not participate in the work-study program are not free teachers.
  C: Some students who participated in the work-study program were enrolled in the fall of 2007.
  D: Some students who participate in work-study activities are not free teachers.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  All free normal students are poor.
  All poor students participated in the work-study program.
  Therefore, all free normal students participated in the work-study program.
  Some students who participated in the work-study program were enrolled in the fall of 2007.
  Therefore, C is true.
  A, B, and D are not necessarily true.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Some of the students enrolled in the fall of 2007 were poor.
Action: Answer("A")

Thought:
  All free teachers are students enrolled in the fall of 2007.
  All free normal students are poor.
  All poor students participate in the work-study program.

  Students who do not participate in the work-study program are not free teachers, which is true as per the statement.
  Some students who participated in the work-study program were enrolled in the fall of 2007, which is also true as per the statement.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Some of the students enrolled in the fall of 2007 were poor.

  A: unconfirmed
  B: 9 people

  Since there are no two people with the same dishes, and there are a total of 9 outcomes per chef, there must be a total of 9 chefs.
  We know that each chef is not more skilled than the others, so we must determine how many pairs of chefs can be compared to each other.

  Therefore, we can only compare chefs in a chain of comparisons, and any chef that is not in the chain cannot be compared to any of the chefs in the chain.
  The maximum length of a chain of comparisons is 3, since any longer chain would violate the condition that no chef can be more skilled than more than one other chef.
  We can start with any chef and compare them to every other chef to determine if they are more skilled.
  If a chef is more skilled than another chef, we add them to the chain.
  If a chef is not more skilled than any other chef in the chain, we start a new chain with that chef.
  After comparing every chef, we count the number of chains to determine how many chefs can be compared to each other without violating the condition.
  By inspection, we can see that there are 3 chains: {1, 2, 3}, {4, 5, 6}, and {7, 8, 9}.
  Therefore, there are 3 chefs who can be compared to each other without violating the condition.

Topic: Logic
Context: A theater plans to perform 7 repertoires in the 7 weeks of the fall, they are F, G., J, K, O, R, S.One repertoire is performed every week, and each repertoire is exactly one week.The repertoire must meet the following conditions? (1) G must be performed in the third week.(2) O and S cannot perform continuously.(3) K must be arranged before J and S.(4) F and J must be arranged to perform in two consecutive weeks.
Question: If S is scheduled for the sixth week, then which week must R be scheduled?
Choices:
  A: the second week
  B: Fourth week
  C: fifth week
  D: Seventh week
Response 0:
Thought: 
  If S is scheduled for the sixth week, then the earliest K can be scheduled is the fourth week.
  Since K must be arranged before J and S, and S is scheduled for the sixth week, then J must be scheduled for the seventh week.
  Since F and J must be arranged to perform in two consecutive weeks, then F must be scheduled for the fifth week.
  Since O and S cannot perform continuously, then O must be scheduled for the fourth week or seventh week.
  Since G must be performed in the third week, then R must be scheduled for the second week.
  Therefore, the answer is A: the second week.

Context: A unit arranges for 6 people on duty on the first day, second day, third day of the new year.They are G., H, K, L, P, and S.Two people are required per day.The personnel arrangement must meet the following conditions? (1) L and P must be on duty on the same day.(2) G and H cannot be on duty on the same day.(3) If K is on the first day of duty, then G is on the second day of duty.(4 ) If S is on the third day of duty, then H is on the second day of duty.
Question: If H is on duty the same day before S, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: G on the second day of duty
  B: P on duty in the second day
  C: K on duty in the first day
  D: H on duty at the first day

  From (1), we know that L and P must be on duty on the same day.

  The remaining people are G and K.
  The only possible arrangement is G and K on duty on the second day and third day, respectively.

Context: A company has six general manager assistants F, G, H, I, M and P, and three departments, each of which is in charge of three general manager assistants.Each assistant general manager is in charge of at least one department.The following conditions must be met? (1) There is only one assistant to the general manager in charge of three departments at the same time.(2) F and G are not in charge of the same department.(3) H and I are not in charge of the same department.
Question: If F and M are not in charge of the same department, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: F and H are in charge of the same department.
  B: F and I are in charge of the same department.
  C: I and P are in charge of the same department.
  D: M and G are in charge of the same department.
Response 0:
Thought:
  There are three departments, each of which is in charge of three general manager assistants. Therefore, there is only one assistant to the general manager in charge of three departments at the same time.
  If F and M are not in charge of the same department, we have two cases:
  Case 1: F is in charge of a department that does not have M
  Case 2: M is in charge of a department that does not have F
  From (2), we know that F and G are not in charge of the same department. Therefore, if F is in charge of a department that does not have M, then G must be in charge of the same department as F. In this case, H and I cannot be in the same department as F and G, so (A) and (B) are false. Since M is not in the same department as F, then (D) is false. Therefore, (C) must be true.
  Case 2: M is in charge of a department that does not have F
  Similar to case 1, we know that G is in charge of the same department as M. In this case, H and I cannot be in the same department as G and M, so (A) and (B) are false. Since F is not in the same department as M, then (D) is false. Therefore, (C) must be true.
  In both cases, (C) is true.

Topic: Logic
Context: When the number of cod in the North Atlantic Ocean decreased significantly, the number of seals increased from 1.5 million to about 2.5 million.Some people think that seals have caused a decrease in cod, but seals rarely eat cod, so it is unlikely that a large increase in the number of seals caused a significant decline in the number of cod.
Question: Which of the following statements, if true, can weaken the argument most strongly?
Choices:
  A: In the traditional cod fishing belt, a large number of seals caused great inconvenience to the fishing boat.
  B: The damage caused by seawater pollution to cod is more serious than that caused to seals.
  C: Before the number of seals increased, the number of cod in the North Atlantic Ocean was greatly reduced.
  D: Cod almost only eat capelin, and this fish is also the main food for seals.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The argument states that seals rarely eat cod, so it is unlikely that a large increase in the number of seals caused a significant decline in the number of cod.
  To weaken the argument, we need a statement that implies seals may have contributed to the decline of cod populations.
  Option A does not provide evidence that seals eat cod, only that they inconvenience fishing boats.
  Option B talks about seawater pollution, but it does not mention seals or cod.
  Option C does not provide evidence that seals eat cod, only that there were fewer cod before the number of seals increased.
  Option D is a strong statement that implies seals and cod compete for the same food source.
  Therefore, Option D is the correct answer.
